Section 1:
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
2 WHEREAS, the General Assembly recognizes a need for an independent tax court
3 or tribunal with its members having expertise in state and local tax matters; and
4 WHEREAS, specialized tax tribunals and courts have been implemented in over 35
5 states, with most housed in the Executive Branch, though some have been placed in the
6 Judicial Branch; and
7 WHEREAS, as currently written, our Constitution would require an amendment to
8 house such a tax tribunal in the Judicial Branch, and therefore, the General Assembly is
9 placing the tax tribunal in the Executive Branch; and
10 WHEREAS, in order to streamline the resolution of all state and local tax-related
11 disputes, the General Assembly intends to and does hereby divest the Circuit Courts and
12 District Courts of original jurisdiction over all such matters vested in the tax tribunal by
13 this Act; and
14 WHEREAS, the General Assembly hereby establishes an independent state-level
15 tax tribunal described and known as the Kentucky Tax Tribunal, which shall have sole
16 and exclusive statewide jurisdiction over all actions that arise under the tax laws in the
17 Commonwealth to hear and resolve all controversies arising out of or related to the
18 assessment, collection, and refund of all state and local taxes in the Commonwealth;
19 NOW, THEREFORE,
20 Be it enacted by the General Assembly of the Commonwealth of Kentucky:
21 SECTION 1. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
22 READ AS FOLLOWS:
23 As used in this Sections 1 to 17 of this Act:
24 (1) "Electronic transmission" includes transmission by facsimile or email;
25 (2) "Taxing agency" includes any state or local cabinet, department, agency,
26 authority, board, commission, school district, special district, municipality, city,
27 county, charter county government, urban-county government, consolidated local
Page 1 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 government, unified local government, or other entity having taxation powers, to
2 the extent each governmental body or entity listed in this subsection levies,
3 assesses, or collects taxes or fees, or has the power to levy, assess, or collect taxes
4 or fees;
5 (3) "Taxpayer" means any person required or permitted by law or administrative
6 regulation to perform any act subject to the administrative jurisdiction of a taxing
7 agency, including the following:
8 (a) File a report, return, statement, certification, claim, estimate, declaration,
9 form, or other document;
10 (b) Furnish any information;
11 (c) Withhold, collect, or pay any tax, installment, estimate, or other funds; and
12 (d) Secure any license, permit, or other authorization to conduct a business or
13 exercise any privilege, right, or responsibility; and
14 (4) "Tribunal" means the Kentucky Tax Tribunal.
15 SECTION 2. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
16 READ AS FOLLOWS:
17 (1) The Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals is abolished on December 31, 2027.
18 (2) (a) The Kentucky Tax Tribunal shall be created in the executive branch
19 effective January 1, 2028.
20 (b) The tribunal shall have exclusive jurisdiction for all tax-related disputes in
21 the Commonwealth.
22 (c) Effective December 31, 2027, the District Courts and Circuit Courts are
23 hereby divested of their original jurisdiction over all civil tax-related matters
24 except any action that may be pending under subsection (6) of this section.
25 (d) The tribunal shall be independent from the authority of all taxing agencies
26 in the Commonwealth and shall rule on all tax-related disputes.
27 (3) In creating the tribunal, the General Assembly intends to foster the settlement or
Page 2 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 other resolution of tax disputes to the greatest extent possible and, in cases in
2 which litigation is necessary, provide the people of the Commonwealth with a fair
3 and independent procedure to resolve tax disputes with taxing agencies. Sections
4 1 to 17 of this Act, including the jurisdiction of the tribunal, shall be interpreted
5 and construed in furtherance of this express legislative intent to secure an
6 efficient, just, speedy, and inexpensive determination or resolution of every tax
7 action.
8 (4) (a) All property of the Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals shall be transferred to
9 the Kentucky Tax Tribunal effective January 1, 2028.
10 (b) All employees of the Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals shall be transferred to
11 the tribunal effective January 1, 2028, without any change in employment
12 status or compensation.
13 (c) Terms of the members of the Board of Tax Appeals shall end upon
14 dissolution of the board on December 31, 2027.
15 (d) All records of the Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals shall be transferred to the
16 tribunal effective January 1, 2028.
17 (5) Sections 1 to 17 of this Act shall apply to:
18 (a) All proceedings commenced before the tribunal on or after January 1,
19 2028;
20 (b) Any pending administrative proceeding involving a question of law or fact
21 arising under any state or local tax law in this Commonwealth, including
22 any action before the Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals, in which a final or
23 nonappealable administrative determination has not been entered before
24 January 1, 2028; and
25 (c) Any action under paragraph (b) of this subsection shall be transferred to
26 the tribunal, which shall render the decision in that proceeding.
27 (6) Sections 1 to 17 of this Act shall not affect any proceeding, prosecution, action,
Page 3 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 suit, or appeal commenced in the judicial branch before January 1, 2028.
2 SECTION 3. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
3 READ AS FOLLOWS:
4 (1) (a) The tribunal shall consist of not more than three (3) judges appointed by the
5 Governor from a list of three (3) persons submitted to him or her by the
6 board of governors of the Kentucky Bar Association.
7 (b) Each appointment made under this subsection shall be:
8 1. For a term of four (4) years; and
9 2. Subject to confirmation by the Senate in accordance with KRS 11.160.
10 (c) From inception of the tribunal forward, if more than one (1) judge is
11 appointed to the tribunal, the judges appointed shall be given terms of
12 differing lengths, not exceeding four (4) years, as may be required to ensure
13 that the terms of office do not expire in the same year.
14 (d) Any vacancy on the tribunal occurring other than by expiration of a term
15 shall be filled in the same manner as an original appointment.
16 (2) (a) Each judge of the tribunal shall be:
17 1. A citizen of the United States;
18 2. A resident of the Commonwealth;
19 3. At least thirty-five (35) years of age; and
20 4. Licensed to practice law in the courts of this Commonwealth for no
21 less than ten (10) continuous years prior to appointment.
22 (b) A person shall not be appointed as a judge of the tribunal unless, at the time
23 of appointment, the individual has demonstrated:
24 1. Extensive knowledge of state and local tax law; and
25 2. Not less than ten (10) years of experience in tax-related dispute
26 resolution and litigation.
27 (3) A judge of the tribunal shall:
Page 4 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 (a) Hold no other public office or position in federal, state, or local government
2 and shall not actively engage in any other gainful employment or business,
3 except nothing in this paragraph shall prohibit a judge of the tribunal from
4 owning a passive interest in business entities or earning income from
5 incidental teaching or scholarly activities;
6 (b) Receive no less than the annual salary and benefits provided to a Circuit
7 Court judge; and
8 (c) Be provided the use of a state-owned motor vehicle.
9 (4) Before assuming the duties of the office, each judge of the tribunal shall take the
10 oath prescribed by Section 228 of the Constitution of Kentucky.
11 (5) (a) If more than one (1) judge is appointed to the tribunal, the Governor shall
12 designate one (1) of the members as the chief judge.
13 (b) The chief judge shall:
14 1. Be the executive of the tribunal;
15 2. Have sole authority over the administration of the tribunal;
16 3. Apportion among the judges all causes, matters, and proceedings
17 coming before the tribunal; and
18 4. Be responsible for the training of all judges appointed to the tribunal
19 by:
20 a. Conducting an orientation session for each judge as
21 expeditiously as possible following his or her appointment; and
22 b. Conducting no less than two (2) seminars each year for all
23 judges and staff of the tax tribunal to discuss any legislative
24 changes, relevant court decisions, and applicable policies and
25 procedures.
26 (6) (a) If the tribunal's docket becomes congested, resulting in the untimely
27 adjudication of claims, or if a judge for any reason cannot preside in an
Page 5 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 action pending before the tribunal and no other judge can preside, the
2 Governor may appoint a special judge.
3 (b) A special judge appointed under this subsection shall:
4 1. Have the same qualifications required in subsection (2) of this section;
5 2. Have all the powers and responsibilities of a regular judge of the
6 tribunal;
7 3. a. Be paid a salary for each day served, not to exceed 1/260 of the
8 annual salary and benefits for a Circuit Judge, and necessary
9 expenses incidental to the performance of the duties of the
10 assignment; or
11 b. In lieu of benefits, a per diem amount equal to the value of
12 benefits calculated in the same manner may be paid at the option
13 of the tribunal; and
14 4. Be entitled to serve for a term no longer than twelve (12) months
15 unless confirmed by the Senate under KRS 11.160.
16 (7) (a) A judge of the tribunal may be removed by the Governor for neglect of duty,
17 misfeasance, malfeasance, or other good cause after being given a copy of
18 the charges and an opportunity for an administrative hearing conducted in
19 accordance with KRS Chapter 13B.
20 (b) Any judge of the tribunal removed by the Governor may appeal any final
21 order of removal to the Franklin Circuit Court in accordance with KRS
22 Chapter 13B.
23 (c) This section shall not preclude the right of any judge removed under this
24 section from pursuing any other remedy provided by law.
25 SECTION 4. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
26 READ AS FOLLOWS:
27 (1) The principal office of the tribunal shall be located in Frankfort, Kentucky, in a
Page 6 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 building that is separate and apart from any building in which a taxing agency is
2 located.
3 (2) (a) The tribunal shall conduct hearings:
4 1. At its principal office; or
5 2. At regional locations throughout the Commonwealth to provide
6 taxpayers a reasonable opportunity to appear before the tribunal with
7 minimal inconvenience and expense. The tribunal, however, shall not
8 conduct hearings at locations that are owned or utilized by taxing
9 agencies for any purpose.
10 (b) 1. Proceedings may also be conducted via video or audio conference; and
11 2. The tribunal, in its discretion, may allow remote attendance at any
12 proceeding.
13 (4) The office of the tribunal shall be open during regular working hours for the
14 conduct of its business, with the exception of closure due to inclement weather or
15 periods of emergency.
16 (5) The tribunal may enter into a memorandum of understanding with the
17 Administrative Office of the Courts to provide hearing rooms, chambers, offices,
18 or other appropriate facilities when hearings are held outside of Frankfort, with
19 the tribunal to bear all incurred costs.
20 SECTION 5. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
21 READ AS FOLLOWS:
22 (1) The tribunal shall have authority to:
23 (a) Hire personnel it determines necessary to carry out its duties and functions;
24 (b) Enter into personal service contracts in compliance with KRS Chapter 45A
25 as needed;
26 (c) Establish a library and obtain any equipment necessary to carry out its
27 duties and functions; and
Page 7 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 (d) Promulgate administrative regulations in accordance with KRS Chapter
2 13A.
3 (2) The records of the tribunal shall be:
4 (a) Maintained in a manner that complies with the confidentiality requirements
5 of Section 30 of this Act, as applicable, and the provisions of KRS 61.870 to
6 61.884; and
7 (b) Retained in the same manner and for the same period of time as records of
8 the Circuit Courts, as published by the Administrative Office of the Courts.
9 SECTION 6. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
10 READ AS FOLLOWS:
11 (1) (a) The tribunal shall have exclusive jurisdiction to hold hearings, make
12 findings of fact, conclusions of law, and issue opinions and orders on all
13 matters arising under any state or local tax law in this Commonwealth.
14 (b) In exercising its exclusive jurisdiction, the tribunal may establish a small
15 claims division and shall have authority to set the jurisdictional limits and
16 procedures of any small claims division.
17 (2) (a) A person shall not contest any matter within the exclusive jurisdiction of the
18 tribunal in any action, suit, or proceeding in the Circuit Court or District
19 Court or any other forum of the Commonwealth except on appeal as
20 provided in subsection (1) of Section 13 of this Act.
21 (b) Any action, suit, or proceeding brought in violation of this subsection shall
22 be dismissed without prejudice by the involved court or forum.
23 (c) The improper commencement of any action, suit, or proceeding shall not
24 toll the time period established for commencing a proceeding before the
25 tribunal.
26 (3) Except in cases involving the denial of a claim for refund credit, offset, or
27 recoupment, the taxpayer shall have the right to have the taxpayer's case heard
Page 8 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 by the tribunal prior to the payment of any contested amount and prior to the
2 posting of any bond required by law.
3 (4) The tribunal shall have jurisdiction over matters where "as-applied" challenges
4 are brought concerning statutes, ordinances, resolutions, administrative
5 regulations, and published policies or rules.
6 (5) A taxpayer desiring to facially challenge the constitutionality of a statute,
7 ordinance, resolution, policy, rule, or administrative regulation as written may, at
8 the taxpayer's election, do so by pursuing one (1) of the following methods, as
9 applicable:
10 (a) 1. Commence a declaratory action with respect to the constitutional
11 challenge in the either the Franklin Circuit Court or the Circuit Court
12 of the county in which the taxpayer resides or maintains a place of
13 business, or, if applicable, the District Courts of the United States; and
14 2. File a petition with the tribunal with respect to the remainder of the
15 matter, which proceeding shall be stayed pending final resolution of
16 the constitutional challenge;
17 (b) File a petition with the tribunal for resolution of all issues other than the
18 constitutional challenge, preserving the constitutional challenge until the
19 entire matter, including the constitutional challenge, is presented to a
20 reviewing appellate court; or
21 (c) Bifurcate the matter by commencing a declaratory action as described in
22 paragraph (a) of this subsection regarding the facial constitutional
23 challenge and filing a petition with the tribunal for a determination of the
24 remaining issues.
25 (6) This section shall not eliminate the board of assessment appeal process embodied
26 in KRS Chapter 133 for property valuation assessment appeals, with all appeals
27 from the board of assessment taken to the tribunal.

1 SECTION 7. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
2 READ AS FOLLOWS:
3 (1) A taxpayer shall commence a proceeding in the tribunal by filing a petition
4 seeking judicial review of a final ruling, order, or other determination of a taxing
5 agency that:
6 (a) Imposes liability for tax, penalty, fee, or interest;
7 (b) Denies a refund, credit application, or claim;
8 (c) Cancels, revokes, suspends, or denies an application for license, permit, or
9 registration related to taxes;
10 (d) Reviews a decision rendered pursuant to Section 36 of this Act; or
11 (e) Constitutes any other action that gives a person the right to a hearing under
12 the tax laws applicable to any taxing agency of the Commonwealth.
13 (2) (a) The petition shall be filed in the tribunal no later than thirty (30) days after
14 the applicable taxing agency's written notice of the final ruling, order, or
15 determination is made and communicated to the taxpayer.
16 (b) The fees required under Section 8 of this Act shall be paid at the time the
17 petition is filed.
18 (3) (a) The taxing agency shall file an answer in the tribunal no later than thirty
19 (30) days after receipt of the tribunal's notification that the taxpayer has
20 properly filed a petition.
21 (b) Upon good cause shown, the tribunal may grant additional time for the
22 taxing agency to file its answer upon motion, not to exceed ninety (90) days.
23 (c) If an amended petition is filed as provided in subsection (6) of this section,
24 the taxing agency shall answer within forty-five (45) days of the filing of the
25 amended petition.
26 (d) The taxing agency shall serve a copy of its answer on the taxpayer and the
27 taxpayer's counsel and file proof of the service with the answer.
Page 10 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 (e) If the taxing agency fails to timely file its answer, all material facts alleged
2 in the petition or amended petition shall be deemed admitted.
3 (4) (a) The taxpayer may file a reply to the agency's answer within fifteen (15) days
4 after receipt of the answer.
5 (b) If an amended answer is made as provided in subsection (6) of this section,
6 the taxpayer shall have thirty (30) days to file a reply.
7 (c) The taxpayer shall serve a copy of the reply on the authorized representative
8 of the taxing agency and shall file proof of service with the reply.
9 (d) If the taxpayer fails to reply within the prescribed time, all material facts
10 alleged in the answer or amended answer shall be deemed admitted.
11 (5) When a reply has been filed, or if no reply has been filed, the matter shall be
12 promptly assigned to a judge and may be scheduled for hearing.
13 (6) (a) Either party may amend a pleading once without leave at any time before
14 the period for responding to the pleading expires.
15 (b) If an answer has been filed, a pleading may be amended only with the
16 written consent of the adverse party or with the permission of the tribunal
17 by order.
18 (7) (a) The parties to a tribunal proceeding may, by written agreement, waive their
19 right to a hearing and submit an action to the tribunal on written
20 stipulations and briefs.
21 (b) After submission, the tribunal may, in its discretion, require appearance for
22 the taking of further evidence or oral argument.
23 (8) Service of process required under this Chapter shall be made in conformity with
24 Section 16 of this Act.
25 SECTION 8. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
26 READ AS FOLLOWS:
27 (1) Upon filing a petition, the taxpayer shall pay to the clerk of the tribunal a filing
Page 11 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 fee, in an amount to be determined by the tribunal, of no less than one hundred
2 dollars ($100) and no more than five hundred dollars ($500) based upon the
3 amount in dispute. All filing fees shall be retained by the tribunal and used as a
4 part of its operating budget.
5 (2) A taxpayer whose petition seeks a hearing in the small claims division established
6 under Section 12 of this Act shall be required to pay a filing fee in the amount of
7 twenty-five dollars ($25).
8 (3) The same fee required for filing a petition under subsection (1) or (2) of this
9 section shall be paid by any other party making an appearance in a proceeding,
10 including an intervenor or amicus curiae, except that no fee shall be charged to a
11 taxing agency, governmental body, or government official appearing in a
12 representative capacity.
13 (4) The tribunal may fix a fee, not in excess of the fees charged and collected by the
14 clerks of the Circuit Courts, for:
15 (a) Compiling documents;
16 (b) Preparing transcripts or any video recording of the record; or
17 (c) Copying any record, entry, or other document, and the compilation and
18 certification of any record, entry, or other document.
19 SECTION 9. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
20 READ AS FOLLOWS:
21 (1) Subject to limitations established by the tribunal in administrative regulations
22 promulgated in accordance with KRS Chapter 13A, a party may obtain discovery
23 by:
24 (a) Written interrogatories;
25 (b) Requests for the production of documents;
26 (c) Depositions; and
27 (d) Requests for admissions.
Page 12 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 (2) The tribunal may provide for other forms of discovery permissible under the
2 Kentucky Rules of Civil Procedure upon motion of a party for good cause shown.
3 (3) A judge or the clerk of the tribunal, on the request of any party to the proceeding,
4 shall issue subpoenas requiring the attendance of witnesses and giving of
5 testimony, and subpoenas duces tecum requiring the production of evidence,
6 consistent with the Kentucky Rules of Civil Procedure.
7 (4) Any witness subpoenaed or whose deposition is taken shall receive from the party
8 requesting their attendance the same fees and mileage as a witness in a Circuit
9 Court proceeding.
10 (5) The tribunal may:
11 (a) Enforce its orders relating to discovery and other procedural issues by
12 deciding issues wholly or partly against the offending party, and:
13 (b) Impose sanctions, including contempt orders, against a party or counsel of
14 record if the violation is found to be willful.
15 (6) The tribunal shall have the authority to award attorney's fees and costs in a
16 manner consistent with the authority of a Circuit Court.
17 SECTION 10. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
18 READ AS FOLLOWS:
19 (1) Proceedings before the tribunal shall be tried de novo, without a jury, and no
20 deference shall be afforded to the taxing agency's action being reviewed.
21 (2) The tribunal shall take evidence, conduct hearings, and issue final and
22 interlocutory decisions.
23 (3) The tribunal shall have the power to review and rule upon motions brought
24 before it and shall have regularly scheduled sessions to hear and rule upon
25 motions by parties, including emergency motions.
26 (4) Testimony shall be given only under oath or affirmation.
27 (5) (a) Absent good cause shown, hearings shall be open to the public and shall be
Page 13 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 conducted in accordance with the rules of practice and procedure as
2 established by the tribunal through administrative regulations promulgated
3 in accordance with KRS Chapter 13A.
4 (b) On motion of either party, the tribunal may issue a protective order or an
5 order closing part or all of the hearing, or seal the record, from the public
6 when the party opposing disclosure of certain information shows good
7 cause to protect the information from disclosure. Any information that the
8 tribunal rules shall not be disclosed shall be exempt from the Open Records
9 Act, KRS 61.870 to 61.884.
10 (c) When deciding whether the moving party has shown good cause to protect
11 information from being disclosed to the public, the judge shall weigh the
12 public's right of access with:
13 1. The privacy rights of participants or third parties;
14 2. Disclosure of trade secrets as defined by KRS 365.880(4); and
15 3. National security.
16 (6) The tribunal shall apply the Kentucky Rules of Evidence in all proceedings,
17 except the tribunal may admit all relevant evidence, including hearsay, if the
18 tribunal determines the evidence is probative of a material fact in controversy.
19 (7) All rules of privilege recognized by the laws of the Commonwealth and common
20 law shall control in the tribunal.
21 (8) In the case of an issue of fact, the taxpayer shall have the burden of proof by a
22 preponderance of the evidence.
23 (9) The taxing agency shall have the burden of proof when attempting to impose
24 findings of penalties, fees, and fraud.
25 (10) Proceedings before the tribunal, except those before the small claims division
26 under Section 12 of this Act, shall be officially reported in a manner consistent
27 with the decisions of the appellate courts of the Commonwealth, with similar
Page 14 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 publication or distribution provisions established by the tribunal.
2 (11) Proceedings before the tribunal shall be conducted in accordance with the
3 provisions of KRS Chapter 13B. To the extent any provision of Sections 1 to 17 of
4 this Act conflicts with the provisions of KRS Chapter 13B, the provisions of
5 Sections 1 to 17 of this Act shall control.
6 (12) (a) The Kentucky Rules of Civil Procedure shall apply to actions before the
7 tribunal.
8 (b) In the case of an appeal from the tribunal under Section 13 of this Act, the
9 Kentucky Rules of Appellate Procedure governing appeals to the Kentucky
10 Court of Appeals shall apply.
11 (c) To the extent any provision of Sections 1 to 17 of this Act conflicts with the
12 Kentucky Rules of Civil Procedure, the provision of Sections 1 to 17 of this
13 Act shall control.
14 (13) Upon motion properly advanced, the petition and other pleadings in the
15 proceeding shall be deemed to conform to the evidence presented at the hearing,
16 unless:
17 (a) A party establishes to the satisfaction of the tribunal that presentation of the
18 evidence would unfairly prejudice the party in maintaining its position on
19 the merits; or
20 (b) Denying the taxpayer's request to conform to the evidence would confer
21 jurisdiction on the tribunal over a matter that would not otherwise come
22 within its jurisdiction.
23 SECTION 11. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
24 READ AS FOLLOWS:
25 (1) (a) The tribunal shall have the power to establish remedies as appropriate for
26 the matter before it.
27 (b) The tribunal shall not have the authority to declare a statute, ordinance,
Page 15 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 resolution, administrative regulation, policy, or rule unconstitutional.
2 (2) The tribunal's decision shall have the same effect and shall be enforced in the
3 same manner as a final judgment of a Circuit Court, unless timely appealed.
4 (3) The tribunal shall render its decisions in writing and shall include a concise
5 statement of the facts found and the conclusions of law reached.
6 (4) The tribunal shall render its decision:
7 (a) No later than six (6) months after submission of the last brief filed following
8 completion of the hearing; or
9 (b) If briefs are not submitted, no later than six (6) months following
10 completion of the hearing and submission of the matter for decision.
11 (5) The chief judge may extend the six (6) month period, for good cause, up to six (6)
12 additional months.
13 (6) If the tribunal fails to render a decision within six (6) months, or twelve (12)
14 months if the chief judge has granted an extension, either party may institute an
15 original action in the Circuit Court to compel issuance of a decision.
16 (7) The tribunal shall apply the doctrine of stare decisis to its decisions, remaining
17 consistent in its application of law from case to case, unless the tribunal provides
18 detailed reasons for distinguishing or reversing its prior precedent.
19 (8) Orders and opinions issued by the Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals, the former
20 Claims Commission, and the former Kentucky Tax Commission may be utilized
21 by the tribunal in its deliberations and decision making. These orders and
22 opinions shall not be binding on the tribunal.
23 (9) The chief judge shall be afforded the opportunity to review and approve all
24 decisions and orders of the tribunal prior to their entry and publication.
25 (10) The tribunal shall promulgate administrative regulations in accordance with KRS
26 Chapter 13A to establish procedures and forms as may be necessary to carry out
27 the implementation, intent, and purposes of Sections 1 to 17 of this Act.
Page 16 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 SECTION 12. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
2 READ AS FOLLOWS:
3 (1) There is hereby created a small claims division of the Kentucky Tax Tribunal.
4 (2) At the direction of the chief judge, the judges of the tribunal shall sit as the
5 judges of the small claims division.
6 (3) (a) The small claims division shall have jurisdiction over any proceeding for:
7 1. Any calendar year, tax year, month, or quarter, where the net amount
8 of the tax deficiencies or claimed refunds in controversy for that time
9 period is at or under twenty-five thousand dollars ($25,000), exclusive
10 of interest, fees, and penalties; and
11 2. All residential real estate ad valorem tax appeals from the board of
12 assessment appeals under Section 36 of this Act.
13 (b) 1. A taxpayer may elect to proceed in the small claims division of the
14 tribunal by filing a petition in the form prescribed by the tribunal for
15 small claims.
16 2. The petition shall be filed no later than thirty (30) days after the
17 applicable agency's written notice of its final ruling, order, or
18 determination is made and communicated to the taxpayer.
19 3. No later than thirty (30) days after service of the petition to proceed in
20 the small claims division, or at any other time as the tribunal may
21 order, the taxing agency shall file with the tribunal an answer and
22 accept or reject the taxpayer's election for the small claims division
23 docket.
24 4. A taxpayer may not revoke an election to proceed in the small claims
25 division once an election has been made.
26 (4) At any time prior to judgment, a taxpayer may voluntarily dismiss a proceeding in
27 the small claims division by notifying the clerk of the request to dismiss the
Page 17 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 proceeding in writing. The dismissal shall be with prejudice.
2 (5) (a) Hearings in the small claims division shall be informal, though judicial
3 decorum shall be maintained at all times.
4 (b) The judge may receive all evidence as he or she deems appropriate for
5 determination of the case.
6 (c) All testimony shall be given under oath or affirmation.
7 (d) A decision from the bench may be issued by the presiding judge if deemed
8 appropriate.
9 (6) A judgment of the small claims division shall not be considered as precedent in
10 any other case, hearing, or proceeding.
11 (7) The taxpayer's election, if accepted by the taxing agency in its answer, shall
12 constitute a waiver of further appeal rights of the parties otherwise afforded
13 under Section 13 of this Act and Section 115 of the Constitution of Kentucky.
14 SECTION 13. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
15 READ AS FOLLOWS:
16 (1) Except as provided in subsection (7) of Section 12 of this Act, a taxpayer or
17 agency shall be entitled to judicial review in the Kentucky Court of Appeals of:
18 (a) A final decision in the form of an opinion or order of the Kentucky Tax
19 Tribunal; or
20 (b) An interlocutory decision of the tribunal which shall be pursued under the
21 same conditions and standards, and in the same manner, as an
22 interlocutory decision of a Circuit Court, including applicable writs.
23 (2) The record on judicial review shall include:
24 (a) The final decision of the tribunal;
25 (b) The stenographic or video transcript of the hearing before the tribunal;
26 (c) The pleadings of record;
27 (d) Any motions submitted by either party; and
Page 18 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 (e) All exhibits, testimony, and documents admitted into evidence.
2 (3) The clerk of the tribunal shall be responsible for producing and certifying the
3 record.
4 SECTION 14. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
5 READ AS FOLLOWS:
6 (1) The following shall apply to appearances in proceedings conducted by the
7 tribunal:
8 (a) If an individual, the taxpayer shall be represented by himself or herself or
9 by an attorney admitted to practice in the Commonwealth; and
10 (b) If not an individual, the taxpayer shall be represented by an attorney
11 admitted to practice in the Commonwealth.
12 (2) Upon motion, the tribunal may allow an attorney not admitted to practice in the
13 Commonwealth to represent a taxpayer when:
14 (a) The attorney is authorized, licensed, and in good standing to practice in his
15 or her original jurisdiction;
16 (b) The taxpayer has retained an attorney admitted to practice in the
17 Commonwealth and that in-state attorney has:
18 1. Entered an appearance in the matter before the tribunal; and
19 2. Complied with all provisions of Kentucky law on pro hac vice
20 admissions, including adequate supervision of out-of-state counsel;
21 and
22 (c) Certified proof given by the submitting attorney of having paid three
23 hundred ten dollars ($310) to the clerk of the tribunal as a fee for the
24 admittance.
25 (3) The taxing agency shall be represented by an authorized attorney of its choosing
26 in all proceedings before the tribunal.

1 READ AS FOLLOWS:
2 Except for decisions issued by the small claims division, the tribunal shall index and

6 SECTION 16. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
7 READ AS FOLLOWS:
8 (1) The following shall constitute personal service on the other party:
9 (a) First class mail, sent to the:
10 1. Taxpayer at the address provided on the petition;
11 2. Taxpayer's attorneys of record; or
12 3. Taxing agency, or its attorney of record.
13 (b) Other means, as prescribed by the tribunal.
14 (2) Mail sent to the tribunal shall be by registered mail, certified mail, return receipt
15 requested, or delivery by a private delivery service approved by the tribunal or by
16 the Internal Revenue Service in accordance with 26 U.S.C. sec. 7502(f). Mailing
17 of any pleading, decision, order, notice, or other documents in respect to
18 proceedings before the tribunal shall be deemed to have occurred on the date
19 deposited with the United States Postal Service as noted by a stamped receipt or
20 postmark confirming the date of mailing or the date of submission to the private
21 delivery service.
22 (3) All filings may be filed with the tribunal by electronic transmission and the filing
23 shall not exceed fifty (50) pages.
24 (4) (a) The party filing a document by electronic transmission shall include a cover
25 page containing the following:
26 1. The date of the transmission;
27 2. The name, address, telephone number, facsimile number if available,
Page 20 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 and email address of the person transmitting the document;
2 3. The caption of the case and case number;
3 4. The name of the judge to whom the case is assigned;
4 5. The title or name of the document; and
5 6. The number of pages transmitted, including the cover page.
6 (b) If a judge or case number has not yet been assigned, that fact shall be stated
7 on the cover page.
8 (5) The sending party shall bear the risk of transmitting a document by electronic
9 transmission to the tribunal.
10 (6) Documents sent and accepted by electronic transmission shall be deemed filed as
11 of the date and time the electronic transmission was received by the tribunal.
12 (7) Electronic transmission filings shall be accepted only during the tribunal's posted
13 regular business hours. Any electronic transmission received after regular
14 business hours on a business day, or on a Saturday, Sunday, or holiday, shall be
15 deemed filed on the next regular business day.
16 (8) A document filed by electronic transmission shall be accepted as the effective,
17 original filing. The submitting party shall file the source document with the
18 tribunal within three (3) business days of submission by electronic transmission.
19 A party filing by electronic transmission shall also serve all other parties to the
20 proceeding by electronic transmission, when feasible.
21 (9) If the electronic transmission includes attachments that cannot be accurately
22 transmitted, or if the enclosure of these attachments would cause the filing to
23 exceed the fifty (50) page limit, each attachment shall be replaced by an inset
24 page describing the attachment and why it is not present. Unless otherwise
25 ordered, the missing attachment shall be filed with the source document
26 submitted to the tribunal.
27 (10) The tribunal may strike any document or attachment which is not filed as
Page 21 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 required by this section.
2 SECTION 17. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
3 READ AS FOLLOWS:
4 (1) (a) An action before the tribunal may be resolved by mediation among the
5 parties by filing a motion for diversion to mediation of an action.
6 (b) The motion may be made by any party within ninety (90) days of the filing
7 of the petition.
8 (c) The tribunal may also order at any time that an action be diverted to
9 mediation on its own motion.
10 (2) The clerk may schedule each action for a mediation conference before a qualified
11 mediator either independently chosen by the parties or appointed by the chief
12 judge, and written notice shall be given to the parties or their attorney by mail.
13 (3) (a) All parties or their attorneys of record scheduled to appear at a mediation
14 conference shall secure settlement authority prior to the conference to
15 respond to settlement proposals that may be offered at the conference.
16 (b) All parties shall be prepared to discuss their positions and explore any
17 possibility of settlement.
18 (c) The costs associated with mediation shall be borne by the parties to the
19 mediation.
20 (4) The chief judge, upon recommendation of the mediator, may enter an order
21 setting forth the action taken or agreement reached at the mediation conference,
22 which, with the consent and agreement of the parties, shall govern the
23 subsequent course of the proceedings.
24 (5) Any action that cannot be resolved through the mediation process shall be
25 scheduled for a hearing.
26 (6) All statements made and information provided by a party at a mediation
27 conference shall be confidential and shall not be disclosed by a party, a party's
Page 22 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 attorney, or the mediator except upon consent of the party.
2 (7) A stenographic record of mediation conferences shall not be taken or maintained.
3 (8) Statements made and information provided in the course of a mediation
4 conference shall not be admissible at a subsequent hearing, except when admitted
5 in accordance with Rule 408 of the Kentucky Rules of Evidence.

19 (1) The Board of Claims may require affected state agencies to investigate claims and

22 specific to support a decision by the board to pay or deny the claim. If the agency
23 believes the state should refute a claim, the agency shall cite the facts about the
24 incident that support its belief.
25 (2) If the claim is under two thousand five hundred dollars ($2,500), it may be
26 investigated by the board in-house and if the board believes it needs additional facts
27 before deciding the claim, the parties may provide the needed information by letter

1 or as directed by the board.
2 (3) The board shall hold hearings on contested claims whose value is two thousand five
3 hundred dollars ($2,500) or greater but may decide claims under two thousand five
4 hundred dollars ($2,500) without a hearing.
5 (4) At its hearings, the board, or any of its members, or any of its hearing officers
6 appointed by the board shall hear the parties at issue and their representatives and
7 witnesses.
8 (5) The award or order shall be made within thirty (30) days after final submission,
9 except in cases involving large or complicated records or unusual questions of law,
10 and shall be made within ninety (90) days after final submission in any event. The
11 order or award, together with a statement of the findings of fact, rulings of law, and
12 other matters pertinent to the question at issue shall be filed with the record of the
13 claim and a copy of the order or award shall immediately be sent to the parties in
14 dispute.
15 (6) In cases over two thousand five hundred dollars ($2,500) that have been assigned to
16 a hearing officer or a member, the hearing officer or member shall tender a
17 recommended order to the full board. The final order in any claim heard by a single
18 member or hearing officer shall be made and entered by a majority of the board.
19 (7) In cases of two thousand five hundred dollars ($2,500) or less decided by a
20 member, a claimant may make an application for review to the full board within
21 fourteen (14) days from the date of the order or award. If an application is made, the
22 full board shall, as soon as practicable, review the evidence, or, if deemed
23 advisable, hear the parties at issue, their representatives and witnesses, and shall
24 make an order or award and file it as specified in subsection (5) above.[

9 (d) The department shall promulgate administrative regulations setting forth the
10 details of the reporting requirements.
11 (14) A tax return shall be filed for each reporting period whether or not tax is due.
12 (15) Any license issued by the department under this section shall not be construed to
13 waive or condone any violation that occurred or may have occurred prior to the
14 issuance of the license and shall not prevent subsequent proceedings against the
15 licensee.
16 (16) (a) The department may deny the issuance of a license under this section if:
17 1. The applicant has made any material false statement on the application
18 for the license; or
19 2. The applicant has violated any provision of KRS 131.600 to 131.630,
20 138.130 to 138.205, 248.754, or 248.756 or any administrative
21 regulations promulgated thereunder.
22 (b) If the department denies the applicant a license under this section, the
23 department shall notify the applicant of the grounds for the denial, and the

1 for the assessment, penalty and interest, and expenses shall be received by the
2 funding commission within thirty (30) days from the date the notice becomes final.
3 The protest shall be accompanied by a supporting statement setting forth the
4 grounds upon which the protest is made. Upon written request, the funding
5 commission may extend the time for filing the supporting statement if it appears the
6 delay is necessary and unavoidable. The refusal of such extension may be reviewed
7 in the same manner as a protested assessment.
8 (2) After a timely protest has been filed, the assessment payer may request a conference
9 with the funding commission. The request shall be granted in writing stating the
10 date and time set for the conference. The assessment payer may appear in person or
11 by representative. Further conferences may be held by mutual agreement.
12 (3) After considering the assessment payer's protest, including any matters presented at
13 the final conference, the funding commission shall issue a final ruling on any matter
14 still in controversy, which shall be mailed to the assessment payer. The ruling shall
15 state that it is a final ruling of the funding commission, generally state the issues in
16 controversy, the funding commission's position thereon and set forth the procedure
17 for prosecuting an appeal to the Kentucky Tax Tribunal[Board of Claims] pursuant
18 to Section 7 of this Act[KRS 49.220].
19 (4) The assessment payer may request in writing a final ruling at any time after filing a
20 timely protest and supporting statement. When a final ruling is requested, the
21 funding commission shall issue such ruling within sixty (60) days or at the next
22 board of directors meeting, whichever is later, from the date the request is received
23 by the funding commission.
24 (5) After a final ruling has been issued, the assessment payer may appeal to the
25 Kentucky Tax Tribunal[Board of Claims] pursuant to Section 7 of this Act[KRS
26 49.220].
27 (6) The expenses incurred by the funding commission in conducting audits required in
Page 122 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 this chapter shall be paid by the audited entities in accordance with administrative
2 regulations promulgated by the funding commission.
3 (7) Notwithstanding any provision to the contrary, a notice of assessment under
4 subsection (1) of this section shall not be collected unless the notice of assessment
5 is mailed to the assessment payer not later than five (5) years from the due date of
6 the quarterly premium report or the date the amended quarterly premium report is
7 filed, whichever is later. A quarterly premium report shall not be amended later
8 than one (1) year after the due date of the quarterly premium report.
9 (8) Assessment payers shall preserve, retain, and provide all documents relevant to
10 quarterly premium reports and subject to audits to the funding commission upon
11 request during the completion of the audit.
12 (9) (a) The funding commission may mail the assessment payer notice of a refund
13 amount to be returned to an insured. The insurance carrier shall pay the
14 amount of the refund to the insured within sixty (60) days from the date of
15 notice sent by the funding commission. If, after good-faith efforts, the refund
16 cannot be returned to the insured, the refund amount shall be remitted to the
17 funding commission within thirty (30) days from the last date of attempting
18 the refund.
19 (b) If a refund amount to an insured is unpaid on the date on which it is due, then
20 that amount shall bear a penalty of one and one-half percent (1.5%) per month
21 from that due date. The funding commission shall have the authority to waive
22 part or all of the penalty where failure to pay is shown, to the satisfaction of
23 the funding commission, to be for a reasonable cause.
24 (10) "Assessment payer" as used in this section means insurance carrier, self-insured
25 group, and self-insured employer.

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 AN ACT relating to the Kentucky Tax Tribunal.
2 WHEREAS, the General Assembly recognizes a need for an independent tax court
3 or tribunal with its members having expertise in state and local tax matters; and
4 WHEREAS, specialized tax tribunals and courts have been implemented in over 35
5 states, with most housed in the Executive Branch, though some have been placed in the
6 Judicial Branch; and
7 WHEREAS, as currently written, our Constitution would require an amendment to
8 house such a tax tribunal in the Judicial Branch, and therefore, the General Assembly is
9 placing the tax tribunal in the Executive Branch; and
10 WHEREAS, in order to streamline the resolution of all state and local tax-related
11 disputes, the General Assembly intends to and does hereby divest the Circuit Courts and
12 District Courts of original jurisdiction over all such matters vested in the tax tribunal by
13 this Act; and
14 WHEREAS, the General Assembly hereby establishes an independent state-level
15 tax tribunal described and known as the Kentucky Tax Tribunal, which shall have sole
16 and exclusive statewide jurisdiction over all actions that arise under the tax laws in the
17 Commonwealth to hear and resolve all controversies arising out of or related to the
18 assessment, collection, and refund of all state and local taxes in the Commonwealth;
19 NOW, THEREFORE,
20 Be it enacted by the General Assembly of the Commonwealth of Kentucky:
21 SECTION 1. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
22 READ AS FOLLOWS:
23 As used in this Sections 1 to 17 of this Act:
24 (1) "Electronic transmission" includes transmission by facsimile or email;
25 (2) "Taxing agency" includes any state or local cabinet, department, agency,
26 authority, board, commission, school district, special district, municipality, city,
27 county, charter county government, urban-county government, consolidated local
Page 1 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 government, unified local government, or other entity having taxation powers, to
2 the extent each governmental body or entity listed in this subsection levies,
3 assesses, or collects taxes or fees, or has the power to levy, assess, or collect taxes
4 or fees;
5 (3) "Taxpayer" means any person required or permitted by law or administrative
6 regulation to perform any act subject to the administrative jurisdiction of a taxing
7 agency, including the following:
8 (a) File a report, return, statement, certification, claim, estimate, declaration,
9 form, or other document;
10 (b) Furnish any information;
11 (c) Withhold, collect, or pay any tax, installment, estimate, or other funds; and
12 (d) Secure any license, permit, or other authorization to conduct a business or
13 exercise any privilege, right, or responsibility; and
14 (4) "Tribunal" means the Kentucky Tax Tribunal.
15 SECTION 2. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
16 READ AS FOLLOWS:
17 (1) The Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals is abolished on December 31, 2027.
18 (2) (a) The Kentucky Tax Tribunal shall be created in the executive branch
19 effective January 1, 2028.
20 (b) The tribunal shall have exclusive jurisdiction for all tax-related disputes in
21 the Commonwealth.
22 (c) Effective December 31, 2027, the District Courts and Circuit Courts are
23 hereby divested of their original jurisdiction over all civil tax-related matters
24 except any action that may be pending under subsection (6) of this section.
25 (d) The tribunal shall be independent from the authority of all taxing agencies
26 in the Commonwealth and shall rule on all tax-related disputes.
27 (3) In creating the tribunal, the General Assembly intends to foster the settlement or
Page 2 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 other resolution of tax disputes to the greatest extent possible and, in cases in
2 which litigation is necessary, provide the people of the Commonwealth with a fair
3 and independent procedure to resolve tax disputes with taxing agencies. Sections
4 1 to 17 of this Act, including the jurisdiction of the tribunal, shall be interpreted
5 and construed in furtherance of this express legislative intent to secure an
6 efficient, just, speedy, and inexpensive determination or resolution of every tax
7 action.
8 (4) (a) All property of the Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals shall be transferred to
9 the Kentucky Tax Tribunal effective January 1, 2028.
10 (b) All employees of the Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals shall be transferred to
11 the tribunal effective January 1, 2028, without any change in employment
12 status or compensation.
13 (c) Terms of the members of the Board of Tax Appeals shall end upon
14 dissolution of the board on December 31, 2027.
15 (d) All records of the Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals shall be transferred to the
16 tribunal effective January 1, 2028.
17 (5) Sections 1 to 17 of this Act shall apply to:
18 (a) All proceedings commenced before the tribunal on or after January 1,
19 2028;
20 (b) Any pending administrative proceeding involving a question of law or fact
21 arising under any state or local tax law in this Commonwealth, including
22 any action before the Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals, in which a final or
23 nonappealable administrative determination has not been entered before
24 January 1, 2028; and
25 (c) Any action under paragraph (b) of this subsection shall be transferred to
26 the tribunal, which shall render the decision in that proceeding.

2 SECTION 3. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
3 READ AS FOLLOWS:
4 (1) (a) The tribunal shall consist of not more than three (3) judges appointed by the
5 Governor from a list of three (3) persons submitted to him or her by the
6 board of governors of the Kentucky Bar Association.
7 (b) Each appointment made under this subsection shall be:
8 1. For a term of four (4) years; and
9 2. Subject to confirmation by the Senate in accordance with KRS 11.160.
10 (c) From inception of the tribunal forward, if more than one (1) judge is
11 appointed to the tribunal, the judges appointed shall be given terms of
12 differing lengths, not exceeding four (4) years, as may be required to ensure
13 that the terms of office do not expire in the same year.
14 (d) Any vacancy on the tribunal occurring other than by expiration of a term
15 shall be filled in the same manner as an original appointment.
16 (2) (a) Each judge of the tribunal shall be:
17 1. A citizen of the United States;
18 2. A resident of the Commonwealth;
19 3. At least thirty-five (35) years of age; and
20 4. Licensed to practice law in the courts of this Commonwealth for no
21 less than ten (10) continuous years prior to appointment.
22 (b) A person shall not be appointed as a judge of the tribunal unless, at the time
23 of appointment, the individual has demonstrated:
24 1. Extensive knowledge of state and local tax law; and
25 2. Not less than ten (10) years of experience in tax-related dispute
26 resolution and litigation.
27 (3) A judge of the tribunal shall:
Page 4 of 125

5 incidental teaching or scholarly activities;
6 (b) Receive no less than the annual salary and benefits provided to a Circuit
7 Court judge; and
8 (c) Be provided the use of a state-owned motor vehicle.

9 SECTION 6. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
10 READ AS FOLLOWS:
11 (1) (a) The tribunal shall have exclusive jurisdiction to hold hearings, make
12 findings of fact, conclusions of law, and issue opinions and orders on all
13 matters arising under any state or local tax law in this Commonwealth.
14 (b) In exercising its exclusive jurisdiction, the tribunal may establish a small
15 claims division and shall have authority to set the jurisdictional limits and
16 procedures of any small claims division.
17 (2) (a) A person shall not contest any matter within the exclusive jurisdiction of the
18 tribunal in any action, suit, or proceeding in the Circuit Court or District
19 Court or any other forum of the Commonwealth except on appeal as
20 provided in subsection (1) of Section 13 of this Act.
21 (b) Any action, suit, or proceeding brought in violation of this subsection shall
22 be dismissed without prejudice by the involved court or forum.
23 (c) The improper commencement of any action, suit, or proceeding shall not
24 toll the time period established for commencing a proceeding before the
25 tribunal.
26 (3) Except in cases involving the denial of a claim for refund credit, offset, or
27 recoupment, the taxpayer shall have the right to have the taxpayer's case heard
Page 8 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 by the tribunal prior to the payment of any contested amount and prior to the
2 posting of any bond required by law.
3 (4) The tribunal shall have jurisdiction over matters where "as-applied" challenges
4 are brought concerning statutes, ordinances, resolutions, administrative
5 regulations, and published policies or rules.
6 (5) A taxpayer desiring to facially challenge the constitutionality of a statute,
7 ordinance, resolution, policy, rule, or administrative regulation as written may, at
8 the taxpayer's election, do so by pursuing one (1) of the following methods, as
9 applicable:
10 (a) 1. Commence a declaratory action with respect to the constitutional
11 challenge in the either the Franklin Circuit Court or the Circuit Court
12 of the county in which the taxpayer resides or maintains a place of
13 business, or, if applicable, the District Courts of the United States; and
14 2. File a petition with the tribunal with respect to the remainder of the
15 matter, which proceeding shall be stayed pending final resolution of
16 the constitutional challenge;
17 (b) File a petition with the tribunal for resolution of all issues other than the
18 constitutional challenge, preserving the constitutional challenge until the
19 entire matter, including the constitutional challenge, is presented to a
20 reviewing appellate court; or
21 (c) Bifurcate the matter by commencing a declaratory action as described in
22 paragraph (a) of this subsection regarding the facial constitutional
23 challenge and filing a petition with the tribunal for a determination of the
24 remaining issues.
25 (6) This section shall not eliminate the board of assessment appeal process embodied
26 in KRS Chapter 133 for property valuation assessment appeals, with all appeals
27 from the board of assessment taken to the tribunal.

1 SECTION 7. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
2 READ AS FOLLOWS:
3 (1) A taxpayer shall commence a proceeding in the tribunal by filing a petition
4 seeking judicial review of a final ruling, order, or other determination of a taxing
5 agency that:
6 (a) Imposes liability for tax, penalty, fee, or interest;
7 (b) Denies a refund, credit application, or claim;
8 (c) Cancels, revokes, suspends, or denies an application for license, permit, or
9 registration related to taxes;
10 (d) Reviews a decision rendered pursuant to Section 36 of this Act; or
11 (e) Constitutes any other action that gives a person the right to a hearing under
12 the tax laws applicable to any taxing agency of the Commonwealth.
13 (2) (a) The petition shall be filed in the tribunal no later than thirty (30) days after
14 the applicable taxing agency's written notice of the final ruling, order, or
15 determination is made and communicated to the taxpayer.
16 (b) The fees required under Section 8 of this Act shall be paid at the time the
17 petition is filed.
18 (3) (a) The taxing agency shall file an answer in the tribunal no later than thirty
19 (30) days after receipt of the tribunal's notification that the taxpayer has
20 properly filed a petition.
21 (b) Upon good cause shown, the tribunal may grant additional time for the
22 taxing agency to file its answer upon motion, not to exceed ninety (90) days.
23 (c) If an amended petition is filed as provided in subsection (6) of this section,
24 the taxing agency shall answer within forty-five (45) days of the filing of the
25 amended petition.
26 (d) The taxing agency shall serve a copy of its answer on the taxpayer and the
27 taxpayer's counsel and file proof of the service with the answer.
Page 10 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 (e) If the taxing agency fails to timely file its answer, all material facts alleged
2 in the petition or amended petition shall be deemed admitted.
3 (4) (a) The taxpayer may file a reply to the agency's answer within fifteen (15) days
4 after receipt of the answer.
5 (b) If an amended answer is made as provided in subsection (6) of this section,
6 the taxpayer shall have thirty (30) days to file a reply.
7 (c) The taxpayer shall serve a copy of the reply on the authorized representative
8 of the taxing agency and shall file proof of service with the reply.
9 (d) If the taxpayer fails to reply within the prescribed time, all material facts
10 alleged in the answer or amended answer shall be deemed admitted.
11 (5) When a reply has been filed, or if no reply has been filed, the matter shall be
12 promptly assigned to a judge and may be scheduled for hearing.
13 (6) (a) Either party may amend a pleading once without leave at any time before
14 the period for responding to the pleading expires.
15 (b) If an answer has been filed, a pleading may be amended only with the
16 written consent of the adverse party or with the permission of the tribunal
17 by order.
18 (7) (a) The parties to a tribunal proceeding may, by written agreement, waive their
19 right to a hearing and submit an action to the tribunal on written
20 stipulations and briefs.
21 (b) After submission, the tribunal may, in its discretion, require appearance for
22 the taking of further evidence or oral argument.
23 (8) Service of process required under this Chapter shall be made in conformity with
24 Section 16 of this Act.

1 (2) The tribunal may provide for other forms of discovery permissible under the

17 SECTION 10. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
18 READ AS FOLLOWS:
19 (1) Proceedings before the tribunal shall be tried de novo, without a jury, and no
20 deference shall be afforded to the taxing agency's action being reviewed.
21 (2) The tribunal shall take evidence, conduct hearings, and issue final and
22 interlocutory decisions.
23 (3) The tribunal shall have the power to review and rule upon motions brought
24 before it and shall have regularly scheduled sessions to hear and rule upon
25 motions by parties, including emergency motions.
26 (4) Testimony shall be given only under oath or affirmation.
27 (5) (a) Absent good cause shown, hearings shall be open to the public and shall be
Page 13 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 conducted in accordance with the rules of practice and procedure as
2 established by the tribunal through administrative regulations promulgated
3 in accordance with KRS Chapter 13A.
4 (b) On motion of either party, the tribunal may issue a protective order or an
5 order closing part or all of the hearing, or seal the record, from the public
6 when the party opposing disclosure of certain information shows good
7 cause to protect the information from disclosure. Any information that the
8 tribunal rules shall not be disclosed shall be exempt from the Open Records
9 Act, KRS 61.870 to 61.884.
10 (c) When deciding whether the moving party has shown good cause to protect
11 information from being disclosed to the public, the judge shall weigh the
12 public's right of access with:
13 1. The privacy rights of participants or third parties;
14 2. Disclosure of trade secrets as defined by KRS 365.880(4); and
15 3. National security.
16 (6) The tribunal shall apply the Kentucky Rules of Evidence in all proceedings,
17 except the tribunal may admit all relevant evidence, including hearsay, if the
18 tribunal determines the evidence is probative of a material fact in controversy.
19 (7) All rules of privilege recognized by the laws of the Commonwealth and common
20 law shall control in the tribunal.
21 (8) In the case of an issue of fact, the taxpayer shall have the burden of proof by a
22 preponderance of the evidence.
23 (9) The taxing agency shall have the burden of proof when attempting to impose
24 findings of penalties, fees, and fraud.
25 (10) Proceedings before the tribunal, except those before the small claims division
26 under Section 12 of this Act, shall be officially reported in a manner consistent
27 with the decisions of the appellate courts of the Commonwealth, with similar
Page 14 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 publication or distribution provisions established by the tribunal.
2 (11) Proceedings before the tribunal shall be conducted in accordance with the
3 provisions of KRS Chapter 13B. To the extent any provision of Sections 1 to 17 of
4 this Act conflicts with the provisions of KRS Chapter 13B, the provisions of
5 Sections 1 to 17 of this Act shall control.
6 (12) (a) The Kentucky Rules of Civil Procedure shall apply to actions before the
7 tribunal.
8 (b) In the case of an appeal from the tribunal under Section 13 of this Act, the
9 Kentucky Rules of Appellate Procedure governing appeals to the Kentucky
10 Court of Appeals shall apply.
11 (c) To the extent any provision of Sections 1 to 17 of this Act conflicts with the
12 Kentucky Rules of Civil Procedure, the provision of Sections 1 to 17 of this
13 Act shall control.
14 (13) Upon motion properly advanced, the petition and other pleadings in the
15 proceeding shall be deemed to conform to the evidence presented at the hearing,
16 unless:
17 (a) A party establishes to the satisfaction of the tribunal that presentation of the
18 evidence would unfairly prejudice the party in maintaining its position on
19 the merits; or
20 (b) Denying the taxpayer's request to conform to the evidence would confer
21 jurisdiction on the tribunal over a matter that would not otherwise come
22 within its jurisdiction.
23 SECTION 11. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
24 READ AS FOLLOWS:
25 (1) (a) The tribunal shall have the power to establish remedies as appropriate for
26 the matter before it.
27 (b) The tribunal shall not have the authority to declare a statute, ordinance,
Page 15 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 resolution, administrative regulation, policy, or rule unconstitutional.
2 (2) The tribunal's decision shall have the same effect and shall be enforced in the
3 same manner as a final judgment of a Circuit Court, unless timely appealed.
4 (3) The tribunal shall render its decisions in writing and shall include a concise
5 statement of the facts found and the conclusions of law reached.
6 (4) The tribunal shall render its decision:
7 (a) No later than six (6) months after submission of the last brief filed following
8 completion of the hearing; or
9 (b) If briefs are not submitted, no later than six (6) months following
10 completion of the hearing and submission of the matter for decision.
11 (5) The chief judge may extend the six (6) month period, for good cause, up to six (6)
12 additional months.
13 (6) If the tribunal fails to render a decision within six (6) months, or twelve (12)
14 months if the chief judge has granted an extension, either party may institute an
15 original action in the Circuit Court to compel issuance of a decision.
16 (7) The tribunal shall apply the doctrine of stare decisis to its decisions, remaining
17 consistent in its application of law from case to case, unless the tribunal provides
18 detailed reasons for distinguishing or reversing its prior precedent.
19 (8) Orders and opinions issued by the Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals, the former
20 Claims Commission, and the former Kentucky Tax Commission may be utilized
21 by the tribunal in its deliberations and decision making. These orders and
22 opinions shall not be binding on the tribunal.
23 (9) The chief judge shall be afforded the opportunity to review and approve all
24 decisions and orders of the tribunal prior to their entry and publication.
25 (10) The tribunal shall promulgate administrative regulations in accordance with KRS
26 Chapter 13A to establish procedures and forms as may be necessary to carry out
27 the implementation, intent, and purposes of Sections 1 to 17 of this Act.

1 SECTION 12. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
2 READ AS FOLLOWS:
3 (1) There is hereby created a small claims division of the Kentucky Tax Tribunal.
4 (2) At the direction of the chief judge, the judges of the tribunal shall sit as the
5 judges of the small claims division.
6 (3) (a) The small claims division shall have jurisdiction over any proceeding for:
7 1. Any calendar year, tax year, month, or quarter, where the net amount
8 of the tax deficiencies or claimed refunds in controversy for that time
9 period is at or under twenty-five thousand dollars ($25,000), exclusive
10 of interest, fees, and penalties; and
11 2. All residential real estate ad valorem tax appeals from the board of
12 assessment appeals under Section 36 of this Act.
13 (b) 1. A taxpayer may elect to proceed in the small claims division of the
14 tribunal by filing a petition in the form prescribed by the tribunal for
15 small claims.
16 2. The petition shall be filed no later than thirty (30) days after the
17 applicable agency's written notice of its final ruling, order, or
18 determination is made and communicated to the taxpayer.
19 3. No later than thirty (30) days after service of the petition to proceed in
20 the small claims division, or at any other time as the tribunal may
21 order, the taxing agency shall file with the tribunal an answer and
22 accept or reject the taxpayer's election for the small claims division
23 docket.
24 4. A taxpayer may not revoke an election to proceed in the small claims
25 division once an election has been made.
26 (4) At any time prior to judgment, a taxpayer may voluntarily dismiss a proceeding in
27 the small claims division by notifying the clerk of the request to dismiss the
Page 17 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 proceeding in writing. The dismissal shall be with prejudice.
2 (5) (a) Hearings in the small claims division shall be informal, though judicial
3 decorum shall be maintained at all times.
4 (b) The judge may receive all evidence as he or she deems appropriate for
5 determination of the case.
6 (c) All testimony shall be given under oath or affirmation.
7 (d) A decision from the bench may be issued by the presiding judge if deemed
8 appropriate.
9 (6) A judgment of the small claims division shall not be considered as precedent in
10 any other case, hearing, or proceeding.
11 (7) The taxpayer's election, if accepted by the taxing agency in its answer, shall
12 constitute a waiver of further appeal rights of the parties otherwise afforded
13 under Section 13 of this Act and Section 115 of the Constitution of Kentucky.
14 SECTION 13. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
15 READ AS FOLLOWS:
16 (1) Except as provided in subsection (7) of Section 12 of this Act, a taxpayer or
17 agency shall be entitled to judicial review in the Kentucky Court of Appeals of:
18 (a) A final decision in the form of an opinion or order of the Kentucky Tax
19 Tribunal; or
20 (b) An interlocutory decision of the tribunal which shall be pursued under the
21 same conditions and standards, and in the same manner, as an
22 interlocutory decision of a Circuit Court, including applicable writs.
23 (2) The record on judicial review shall include:
24 (a) The final decision of the tribunal;
25 (b) The stenographic or video transcript of the hearing before the tribunal;
26 (c) The pleadings of record;
27 (d) Any motions submitted by either party; and
Page 18 of 125

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 (e) All exhibits, testimony, and documents admitted into evidence.
2 (3) The clerk of the tribunal shall be responsible for producing and certifying the
3 record.
4 SECTION 14. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
5 READ AS FOLLOWS:
6 (1) The following shall apply to appearances in proceedings conducted by the
7 tribunal:
8 (a) If an individual, the taxpayer shall be represented by himself or herself or
9 by an attorney admitted to practice in the Commonwealth; and
10 (b) If not an individual, the taxpayer shall be represented by an attorney
11 admitted to practice in the Commonwealth.
12 (2) Upon motion, the tribunal may allow an attorney not admitted to practice in the
13 Commonwealth to represent a taxpayer when:
14 (a) The attorney is authorized, licensed, and in good standing to practice in his
15 or her original jurisdiction;
16 (b) The taxpayer has retained an attorney admitted to practice in the

18 1. Entered an appearance in the matter before the tribunal; and
19 2. Complied with all provisions of Kentucky law on pro hac vice
20 admissions, including adequate supervision of out-of-state counsel;
21 and
22 (c) Certified proof given by the submitting attorney of having paid three
23 hundred ten dollars ($310) to the clerk of the tribunal as a fee for the
24 admittance.
25 (3) The taxing agency shall be represented by an authorized attorney of its choosing
26 in all proceedings before the tribunal.

11 2. Taxpayer's attorneys of record; or
12 3. Taxing agency, or its attorney of record.
13 (b) Other means, as prescribed by the tribunal.
14 (2) Mail sent to the tribunal shall be by registered mail, certified mail, return receipt
15 requested, or delivery by a private delivery service approved by the tribunal or by
16 the Internal Revenue Service in accordance with 26 U.S.C. sec. 7502(f). Mailing
17 of any pleading, decision, order, notice, or other documents in respect to
18 proceedings before the tribunal shall be deemed to have occurred on the date
19 deposited with the United States Postal Service as noted by a stamped receipt or
20 postmark confirming the date of mailing or the date of submission to the private
21 delivery service.
22 (3) All filings may be filed with the tribunal by electronic transmission and the filing
23 shall not exceed fifty (50) pages.
24 (4) (a) The party filing a document by electronic transmission shall include a cover
25 page containing the following:
26 1. The date of the transmission;
27 2. The name, address, telephone number, facsimile number if available,
Page 20 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 and email address of the person transmitting the document;
2 3. The caption of the case and case number;
3 4. The name of the judge to whom the case is assigned;
4 5. The title or name of the document; and
5 6. The number of pages transmitted, including the cover page.
6 (b) If a judge or case number has not yet been assigned, that fact shall be stated
7 on the cover page.
8 (5) The sending party shall bear the risk of transmitting a document by electronic
9 transmission to the tribunal.
10 (6) Documents sent and accepted by electronic transmission shall be deemed filed as
11 of the date and time the electronic transmission was received by the tribunal.
12 (7) Electronic transmission filings shall be accepted only during the tribunal's posted
13 regular business hours. Any electronic transmission received after regular
14 business hours on a business day, or on a Saturday, Sunday, or holiday, shall be
15 deemed filed on the next regular business day.
16 (8) A document filed by electronic transmission shall be accepted as the effective,
17 original filing. The submitting party shall file the source document with the
18 tribunal within three (3) business days of submission by electronic transmission.
19 A party filing by electronic transmission shall also serve all other parties to the
20 proceeding by electronic transmission, when feasible.
21 (9) If the electronic transmission includes attachments that cannot be accurately
22 transmitted, or if the enclosure of these attachments would cause the filing to
23 exceed the fifty (50) page limit, each attachment shall be replaced by an inset
24 page describing the attachment and why it is not present. Unless otherwise
25 ordered, the missing attachment shall be filed with the source document
26 submitted to the tribunal.
27 (10) The tribunal may strike any document or attachment which is not filed as
Page 21 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 required by this section.
2 SECTION 17. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 142 IS CREATED TO
3 READ AS FOLLOWS:
4 (1) (a) An action before the tribunal may be resolved by mediation among the
5 parties by filing a motion for diversion to mediation of an action.
6 (b) The motion may be made by any party within ninety (90) days of the filing
7 of the petition.
8 (c) The tribunal may also order at any time that an action be diverted to
9 mediation on its own motion.
10 (2) The clerk may schedule each action for a mediation conference before a qualified
11 mediator either independently chosen by the parties or appointed by the chief
12 judge, and written notice shall be given to the parties or their attorney by mail.
13 (3) (a) All parties or their attorneys of record scheduled to appear at a mediation
14 conference shall secure settlement authority prior to the conference to
15 respond to settlement proposals that may be offered at the conference.
16 (b) All parties shall be prepared to discuss their positions and explore any
17 possibility of settlement.
18 (c) The costs associated with mediation shall be borne by the parties to the
19 mediation.
20 (4) The chief judge, upon recommendation of the mediator, may enter an order
21 setting forth the action taken or agreement reached at the mediation conference,
22 which, with the consent and agreement of the parties, shall govern the
23 subsequent course of the proceedings.
24 (5) Any action that cannot be resolved through the mediation process shall be
25 scheduled for a hearing.
26 (6) All statements made and information provided by a party at a mediation
27 conference shall be confidential and shall not be disclosed by a party, a party's
Page 22 of 125
XXXX 2/12/2026 8:42 PM Jacketed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS BR 1803
1 attorney, or the mediator except upon consent of the party.
2 (7) A stenographic record of mediation conferences shall not be taken or maintained.
3 (8) Statements made and information provided in the course of a mediation
4 conference shall not be admissible at a subsequent hearing, except when admitted
5 in accordance with Rule 408 of the Kentucky Rules of Evidence.

22 part or all of the penalty where failure to pay is shown, to the satisfaction of
23 the funding commission, to be for a reasonable cause.
24 (10) "Assessment payer" as used in this section means insurance carrier, self-insured
25 group, and self-insured employer.
